IN THE SUPREME COURT OF INDIA
CIVIL APPELLATE JURISDICTION
CIVIL APPEAL NO.           OF 2026
   (Arising out of SLP (Civil) No.19210 OF 2025)
THE BOMBAY PRESIDENCY GOLF CLUB LIMITED  APPELLANT(S)
                             VERSUS
SUCHETA DESMOND RODRIGUES & ORS.        RESPONDENT(S)
O R D E R
1. Leave granted.
2. The appellant challenges the impugned judgment
and order dated 11.06.2025 in First Appeal No.1568
of 2024 in Suit No.3054 of 2018, titled “ Sucheta
Desmond Rodrigues Vs. The Bombay Presidency Golf
Club Limited and Ors.”, passed by the High Court of
Judicature at Bombay.
3. We have heard learned counsel for the parties
and perused the material available on record.
4. Learned counsel for the parties submitted
that all the disputes and differences between the
parties  have  been  amicably  resolved,  and  the
parties have decided to part ways on the mutually
agreed  terms.  Accordingly,  appropriate  and
1

--- Page 8 ---
necessary  orders  may  be  passed  in  accordance
therewith.
5. We place on record with satisfaction the
efforts put in by Mr. Pranjal Kishore, learned
counsel, Mr. Sanyat Lodha, learned counsel, and
also the other learned senior counsel(s), who had
helped  the  parties  to  arrive  at  an  amicable
settlement. The terms of the settlement stands
reduced into writing vide document (Consent Terms)
dated 02.06.2026, duly signed by all the concerned
is taken on record.
6. The terms of the settlement (Consent Terms)
reads as under:
“6. With the view to amicably resolve their
disputes, the Parties have agreed to the
following terms: 
TERMS AND CONDITIONS

families are residing in the subject property with
approximately 3000 inhabitants.

the judgment of the High Court shall not be treated
as a precedent.

--- Page 33 ---
The  applicant/appellant  seeks  suspension  of
sentence, during the pendency of the present appeal.
The appellant has been convicted for the offences
punishable under Section 3(3) of t he Terrorist and
Disruptive Activities (Prevention) Act, 1987 (for
short, the TADA  Act) read with Section 120B of the
Indian Penal Code, and he was sentenced to undergo
rigorous imprisonment for a period of five years
along with fine. 
Admittedly,  out  of  the  sentence  of  five
years  which  has  been  awarded,  the
applicant/appellant  has  already  undergone
incarceration for a period of three years and nine
months.  The  appeal  is  also  likely  to  take
substantial time for its disposal.
Considering the above circumstances, we are
inclined to suspend the sentence awarded to the
applicant/appellant and grant bail to him, during
the pendency of the present appeal.
Accordingly, the sentence imposed upon the
applicant/appellant  stands  suspended,  and  he  is
granted regular bail, during the pendency of the
appeal, subject to the terms and conditions that may
be imposed by the concerned Trial Court
2

--- Page 34 ---
The applications are allowed, accordingly. 
List the appeal in due course.

IN THE SUPREME COURT OF INDIA
CRIMINAL APPELLATE JURISDICTION
CRIMINAL APPEAL NO.        OF 2026
(Arising out of SLP (Crl.) No. 6211 of 2026)
SARASWATI SAHU   APPELLANT(S)
VERSUS
STATE OF CHHATTISGARH   RESPONDENT(S)
O R D E R
1. Leave granted.
2. Heard learned counsel for the parties.
3. This  appeal  arises  from  an  order  dated
16.02.2026 passed by the High Court of Chhattisgarh
rejecting the regular bail prayer of the appellant in
connection with FIR No. 480, Police Station Kharsia
(Chowki  Jobi),  District  Raigarh  (State  of
Chhattisgarh).
4. The submission on behalf of the appellant is
that there is no incriminating recovery from the
appellant; and her complicity has come to light basis
a confessional statement of the co-accused which does
not have evidentiary value. It has been submitted
that the appellant is a lady, who has suffered
incarceration since 28.08.2025 and is not likely to
1

--- Page 51 ---
misuse the bail, if released.
5. The learned counsel for the State has opposed
the prayer for bail but could not dispute that there
is no incriminating recovery from the appellant.
6. Having  regard  to  the  aforesaid  submissions,
without expressing any opinion on the merits of the
prosecution  case,  we  are  of  the  view  that  the
appellant is entitled to be released on bail at this
stage.
7.  Accordingly, the appeal is allowed. The order
passed by the High Court rejecting the regular bail
prayer of the appellant is set aside.
8. The appellant shall be released on bail on such
terms and conditions as the trial court may deem fit
to impose in the facts and circumstances of the case.
9. Pending  application(s),  if  any,  shall  stand
disposed of.
  
 ………………………………………………………J.
             [MANOJ MISRA]
   
  ………………………………………………………J.
       [SHREE CHANDRASHEKHAR]
NEW DELHI;
8 July, 2026
2

1. The submission on behalf of
the petitioner is that FIR No. 4 of
2022 at PS Gumanpura, District-Kota
City  was  lodged,  against  the
petitioner and 37 other co-accused,
alleging  offences  punishable  under
sections  420  and  406  IPC.  It  was
alleged  in  the  first  information
report  that  accused  had  solicited
investments  in  their  group  of
companies,  and  have  diverted  the
funds,  resulting  in  losses  to  the
investors. With similar allegations,
several other FIRs, details of which
are provided in paragraph 3 of the
writ petition filed before the High
Court,  were  lodged.  In  several  of
those  FIRs,  the  petitioner  was
admitted to bail. However, as those
2

--- Page 56 ---
FIRs were multiplying, and were based
on  identical  allegations,  writ
petition was filed before the High
court seeking clubbing of all FIRs
and  joint  investigation  as  they
related to the same offence. During
pendency of the said writ petition,
an  application  was  submitted  for
interim protection, which came to be
rejected by the impugned order.
2. It  is  the  case  of  the
petitioner that similar petitions by
various accused were filed before the
High  court,  i.e.  criminal  writ
petition  Nos.  575/2023,  882/2022,
303/2023,  576/2023  and  1132/2023,

on 29.03.2023, and thereafter another
interim  order  was  passed  on
25.05.2023. It is the case of the
petitioner  that  those  similar
3

--- Page 57 ---
petitions  are  still  pending,  and
therefore similar protection ought to
have been accorded to the petitioner.

six weeks.
4. In  the  meantime,  it  is
provided  that  the  petitioner  shall
not be arrested in connection with
any such FIR which makes allegations
identical to the one in FIR No.4 of
2022, Gumanpura, District-Kota City.
5. It  is,  however,  made  clear
that the petitioner shall cooperate
in the investigation.

IN THE SUPREME COURT OF INDIA
CIVIL APPELLATE JURISDICTION
CIVIL APPEAL NOS.         /2026  
(@ SLP(C) Nos. 20402-20403/2025)
LABH SINGH                                    Appellant(s)
                                VERSUS
     NILOKHERI MUNICIPALITY NILOKHERI & ANR.       Respondent(s)
O R D E R
   1. Leave granted.
2. Heard learned counsel for the parties.
3. These appeal(s) arise from an order of the High
Court, dated 09.04.2025, passed in RSA No. 594/1993,
whereby the High Court dismissed the Second Appeal for
non-prosecution. The appellant also impugns the order
dated  28.04.2025  by  which  appellant’s  application
seeking restoration of the Second Appeal was dismissed.
4. The submission on behalf of the appellant is
that the High Court had considered the order sheet of
the appeal to infer that the appellant had not been
interested in pursuing the second appeal as it had been
pending  since  1993,  and  on  numerous  occasion  the
counsel for the appellant had not appeared in the
proceedings. According to the appellant, the High Court
ought to have considered whether the appellant had
1

--- Page 59 ---
submitted sufficient explanation for his non-appearance
on the date when the matter was dismissed for non-
prosecution.  It  is  submitted  that  the  restoration
application was submitted within time, and satisfactory
explanation was offered for non-appearance on the date
when the matter was dismissed for non-prosecution. In
such circumstances, according to the learned counsel
for the appellant, the second appeal ought to have been
restored for decision on merits.
5. The  learned  counsel  appearing  for  the
respondents though opposed the prayer of the appellant
but could not demonstrate that the High Court had
accorded due consideration to the explanation offered
in the restoration application.
6. Having regard to the facts of the case as also
that it is always in the interest of justice to
adjudicate the matter on merits, if the parties are
willing to cooperate in the hearing of the matter,
while  taking  into  consideration  that  restoration
application offering explanation for non-appearance on
the date concerned was submitted within the period of
limitation, we are of the view that the High Court
ought to have allowed the restoration application and
restore the appeal on the file for a decision in
accordance with law.
7. Accordingly, these appeal(s) are allowed . The order
dated 28.04.2025 rejecting the restoration application
2

--- Page 60 ---
is set aside. The restoration application is allowed
and,  consequently,  the  order  dated  09.04.2025
dismissing the appeal for non-prosecution is set aside.
As a result, RSA No. 594/1993 shall stand restored on
the record of the High Court for being decided afresh
in accordance with the law.  Pending applications, if
any, shall stand disposed of.
……………………………………………………………………….J.
[MANOJ MISRA]

1. We have heard Mr. Guru Krishna Kumar, Mr. Sajan Poovayya,
learned  Senior  Counsels  for  the  petitioner(s),
Mr.P.S.Patwalia, Mr. Siddharth Aggarwal, Ms. Swathi Sukumar,
learned Senior Counsels for the respondents.
2. The impugned judgment is a judgment of reversal. The
plaintiff(s) is in appeal before us. The plaintiff’s case is
that the patent in question is a Standard Essential Patents
(SEP) and that the plaintiff(s) was prepared to license under
the Fair, Reasonable, and Non-Discriminatory -‘FRAND’ terms to
the respondent(s).
3. However, according to the plaintiff(s), the defendant(s)
refused  the  ‘ FRAND’ arrangement.  According  to  the
plaintiff(s), there was infringement of the patent.
4. All  this  is  disputed  by  the  defendant(s).  The
defendant(s) have raised multifarious defences to contend that
the patent is not a Standard Essential Patents (SEP); that
there was no infringement and they have also relied on the
principle of exhaustion to contend that the suit and the
reliefs claimed are not maintainable.
5. Having considered the matter(s) and the arguments, we are

--- Page 64 ---
3
of opinion that the matters requires a detailed consideration.
6. Issue notice to the respondent(s), returnable on 11 th
August, 2026.
7. Let pleadings be completed. 
8. In the meantime, the arrangement that prevailed before
the Division Bench of the High Court for the past 08 years,
namely, ‘that the petitioner(s) would keep the Bank Guarantee
alive’ shall continue.
9. We direct that the petitioner(s), till further orders,
shall keep the Bank Guarantee alive.
10. Mr. Guru Krishna Kumar, learned Senior Counsel for the
petitioner(s) undertakes, in the event of the impugned orders
being sustained and the petitioner(s) losing the appeal(s),
they will reimburse the respondent(s) with the upto date
amount.
11. Necessary undertaking in this regard be filed within a
period of one week from today.
12. Further proceedings, in the High Court for restitution to
remain stayed.
13. List the matters on 11th August, 2026.

         HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE SHEEL NAGU
    [PARTIAL COURT WORKING DAYS BENCH]
For Petitioner(s)  Mr. Aayushman Jauhari, Adv.

                   Mr. Towseef Ahmad Dar, AoR
                   
For Respondent(s) 
          
                             O R D E R
Heard learned counsel for the petitioner.
2. Delay condoned.

--- Page 69 ---
2
3. The petitioner is aggrieved by the impugned order dated
16.01.2026 passed by the High Court of Judicature at Allahabad in
Writ Tax No.1142 of 2024, by which the High Court has not
interfered in the matter on the ground that now the GST Appellate
Tribunal has started functioning and the matter is required to be
considered by the said Appellate Tribunal.
4. However, learned counsel for the petitioner submitted that as
per the latest material available on the website of the GST
Appellate Tribunal, the same has not yet fully functional for the
reason that the cases have not even been registered/numbered.
5. Having regard to the aforesaid and taking into consideration
the fact that, the GST Appellate Tribunal has specifically been
constituted to lessen the load of the High Court in such matters
for a specific purpose and the same has become functional, we
expect that the same would start functioning fully also.
6. Accordingly, the Special Leave Petition stands disposed of
with liberty to the petitioner to mention the matter before the
President  of  the  GST  Appellate  Tribunal  for  not  only
registering/numbering the case but also to take up the matter and
if required, at least hear it for the purpose of any interim relief
which the petitioner may require.
7. We are conscious that the GST Appellate Tribunal because of
its recent constitution and functioning, may be overloaded but in
the peculiar facts and circumstances of the present case, when the
matter was at the final stage before the High Court, we find it to
be an appropriate case where a discretion for priority hearing of
the case of the petitioner is required to be exercised. We have no

--- Page 70 ---
3
doubt that the President of the GST Appellate Tribunal would take
appropriate action in the matter, if the matter is so mentioned.
8. Pending application(s), if any, shall also stand disposed of.
(SAPNA BISHT)                                   (ANJALI PANWAR)

and have perused the record.

view  that  this  Transfer  Petition  deserves  to  be
allowed.  Accordingly,  M.C.  1533/2025,  titled  as

the  Principal  Judge,  Family  Court  at  Bangalore,
1

--- Page 78 ---
Karnataka  is  transferred  to  Family  Court  at
Bhubaneshwar. The transferor Court shall transmit the
entire record of the case forthwith to the transferee
Court.

appropriate to observe that it will be open to the
parties to appear through video conferencing platform
except on occasions where their physical presence is
necessary. 
5. The Transfer Petition is allowed in the above
terms.

disposed of.

O R D E R
Heard Mr. Maninder Singh, learned senior counsel and Mr. Rahul
Mehra, learned senior counsel appearing for the petitioner.
2. Learned senior counsel for the petitioner submits that the
present matters were mentioned day before yesterday i.e., on
07.07.2026 before this Court, being the senior most Bench available
during the partial court working days and the same was allowed and
the matters were directed to be listed today before an appropriate
Bench and the Bench before which the matters were listed today, one
of the Hon’ble Judges (Justice K.V. Viswanathan) has recused
himself from hearing and has directed him to take steps for early
listing.
